<div id="review_1178171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1178171" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1178171?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780679435204" href="/book/show/855708.Bird_By_Bird">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">writers and readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=biography">biography</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=1-also-at-librarything">1-also-at-librarything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-female-author-or-illust">readbooks-female-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=essays">essays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1178171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5574630390689679925">This is an enjoyable read and a lovely book. Anne Lamott is a very engaging writer and she is very funny, honest, and heartfelt. Although I don’t desire to be a writer, like most readers I’ve wanted to be a writer at times in my life. I took to heart her advice that at some point one has to decide whether to be a reader or a writer, a choice I’d made but it solidified my decision for me. The “bird by bird” philosophy espoused in this book can apply to all endeavors, not just the one of writing.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_16602560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16602560" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/236411-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291695844p2/236411.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16602560?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/236411-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16602560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11025243272365009439">I can see why this is a popular book. Lamott is funny, self-deprecating, and encouraging even in the face of cold, hard realities. She means what she says in the title, too. It really does set out to be instructions on writing and life. There are undoubtedly better books covering particulars of the craft, but this may be one of the best at construing a writer’s perspective. I liked her advice about making incremental progress (the meaning of “bird by bird”), about getting something/anything down</span>
  <span id="freeText11025243272365009439" style="display:none">I can see why this is a popular book. Lamott is funny, self-deprecating, and encouraging even in the face of cold, hard realities. She means what she says in the title, too. It really does set out to be instructions on writing and life. There are undoubtedly better books covering particulars of the craft, but this may be one of the best at construing a writer’s perspective. I liked her advice about making incremental progress (the meaning of “bird by bird”), about getting something/anything down that can then be refined in later drafts, and about finding characters, plot, voice, and truth from distinct parts of yourself. She also made clear how writing can make you a more appreciative reader. <br />Another bit of advice Lamott offered rang true: readers want to like the storyteller. I would say she achieved most of that goal herself as she laid out the story of her own literary life. Every once in a while it seemed like she had favorite anecdotes she shoehorned into the narrative that didn’t quite fit, but that’s a small quibble. A slightly bigger gripe from my own point of view was that there were times where it felt like she was leading a touchy-feely seminar on self-actualization. Having never been to one, I’m only guessing here, but it seemed like a peculiarity we might expect from certain kinds of Californians. I didn’t allow this to detract from the experience, though. Nor should you if you’re looking for writing/life instruction of a semi-practical, semi-inspirational sort.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11025243272365009439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1594016166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11213403833773147101">Anne Lamott has made me finally feel like it is all going to be okay!<br/><br/>This is less of an instructional guide to the craft of writing and more of an extended pep-talk about living life creatively. This book will not necessarily guide you in how to create stellar characters or how to merge your sub-plot with your main plot-line, but it will aid you in going into your writing endeavors with a more sound mind and a better expectation of what the creative process holds. It is profound, anecdotal and f</span>
  <span id="freeText11213403833773147101" style="display:none">Anne Lamott has made me finally feel like it is all going to be okay!<br /><br />This is less of an instructional guide to the craft of writing and more of an extended pep-talk about living life creatively. This book will not necessarily guide you in how to create stellar characters or how to merge your sub-plot with your main plot-line, but it will aid you in going into your writing endeavors with a more sound mind and a better expectation of what the creative process holds. It is profound, anecdotal and full of wry observations about life being somewhere between faith and failure. Perfectionism is seen as the root of all evil and kudos is paid to "the shitty first draft".<br /><br />Her conversational, witty and engaging tone has allowed me to believe in myself whilst dually giving the hard facts about life as a writer. She doesn't sugar-coat and she doesn't dress anything up, but she does give hope and she does urge every writer-to-be to own their own voice and to strive for the stories within themselves.<br /><br />This is a must-read for both amateur and professional writers, as well as all those with an interest in creative living.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11213403833773147101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79885934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer347333589385015455">Very inspirational reread of a book I remember loving many years ago. This time I listened to it in audio. Susan Bennett did such a good job I believed I was listening to Anne Lamott. I love Lamott's authenticity, her personal anecdotes, her humor and her advise. I simply like her. Lamott puts so much of herself into this book that I feel like she is a friend whom I could meet for coffee and just start gabbing about life. I imagine that she has this effect on many of her readers.<br/><br/> I'm not a write</span>
  <span id="freeText347333589385015455" style="display:none">Very inspirational reread of a book I remember loving many years ago. This time I listened to it in audio. Susan Bennett did such a good job I believed I was listening to Anne Lamott. I love Lamott's authenticity, her personal anecdotes, her humor and her advise. I simply like her. Lamott puts so much of herself into this book that I feel like she is a friend whom I could meet for coffee and just start gabbing about life. I imagine that she has this effect on many of her readers.<br /><br /> I'm not a writer but it was interesting to hear what she had to say to writers. Plus, her advice and philosophy can be applied to anything in life. I think I read this the first time while overwhelmed working on my doctoral dissertation. Lamott's father's advice to his overwhelmed grandson to work on his project one bird at a time, "bird by bird, " was very calming and useful advice for me at that time. I've never forgotten that anecdote or advice. <br /><br />My only negative which isn't a reflection on the book, is that some of the advice felt old. I'm older by about 25-30 years so that accounts for that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="347333589385015455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="My_Strange_Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="My_Strange_Reading" href="/user/show/29983165-my-strange-reading">My_Strange_Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29983165-my-strange-reading?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29983165-my-strange-reading?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1590594770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3471593290442446422">#mystrangereading bird by bird by Anne Lamott ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/>"Perfectionism is the voice of the oppressor, the enemy of the people. It will keep you cramped and insane your whole life, and or is the main obstacle between you and your shitty first draft"<br/><br/>"One of the things that happens when you give yourself permission to start writing is that you start thinking like a writer"<br/><br/>I'm so thankful that my Aunt Robin recommended this book yesterday! How have I missed it? It's such a great encouragement for so</span>
  <span id="freeText3471593290442446422" style="display:none">#mystrangereading bird by bird by Anne Lamott ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />"Perfectionism is the voice of the oppressor, the enemy of the people. It will keep you cramped and insane your whole life, and or is the main obstacle between you and your shitty first draft"<br /><br />"One of the things that happens when you give yourself permission to start writing is that you start thinking like a writer"<br /><br />I'm so thankful that my Aunt Robin recommended this book yesterday! How have I missed it? It's such a great encouragement for someone who has started playing with writing recently. I love the short chapters, the practical advice and the realistic expectations that she sets. It's wonderful and I recommend for anyone who is taking on something new that they haven't tried before. It doesn't just apply to writing! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3471593290442446422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer937274469163202748">This book is like a friend to me. Anne Lamott advises and encourages towards writing as a way of life. She helps the reader understand the various aspects of writing and also in introspecting and finding one's own voice. This is a book that I'm gonna read over and over again. I love it. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XGXGl/ltRKDgvy4O5dUtyPccYlAGbuy1XuSGYcxVA7N+2rhN6qil+RLYnKTrdji2WKNCVy/FyoU1snXPtG1olg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nJQKOpNOokpJPNd2GTn6Dvb1viYNIIR3MZ8WuBiP2Na+K3TggItDE7tbZdwXmu9wWUqeISSLokdayeUWYLez8w==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7113.Anne_Lamott">About Anne Lamott</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7113.Anne_Lamott"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1489601640p3/7113.jpg);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/7113.Anne_Lamott">Anne Lamott
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11918148877709858262">Anne Lamott is an author of several novels and works of non-fiction. Based in the San Francisco Bay Area, her non-fiction works are largely autobiographical, with strong doses of self-deprecating humor and covering such subjects as alcoholism, single motherhood, and Christianity. She appeals to her fans because of her sense of humor, her deeply felt insights, and her outspoken views on topics such</span>
  <span id="freeText11918148877709858262" style="display:none">Anne Lamott is an author of several novels and works of non-fiction. Based in the San Francisco Bay Area, her non-fiction works are largely autobiographical, with strong doses of self-deprecating humor and covering such subjects as alcoholism, single motherhood, and Christianity. She appeals to her fans because of her sense of humor, her deeply felt insights, and her outspoken views on topics such as her left-of-center politics and her unconventional Christian faith. She is a graduate of Drew College Preparatory School in San Francisco, California. Her father, Kenneth Lamott, was also a writer and was the basis of her first novel <i>Hard Laughter</i>.<br /><br />Lamott's life is documented in Freida Lee Mock's 1999 documentary <i>Bird by Bird: A Film Portrait of Writer Anne Lamott</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11918148877709858262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/841198-bird-by-bird-some-instructions-on-writing-and-life">Quotes from Bird by Bird: Som...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;For some of us, books are as important as almost anything else on earth. What a miracle it is that out of these small, flat, rigid squares of paper unfolds world after world after world, worlds that sing to you, comfort and quiet or excite you. Books help us understand who we are and how we are to behave. They show us what community and friendship mean; they show us how to live and die.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/44140-for-some-of-us-books-are-as-important-as-almost">2076 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Perfectionism is the voice of the oppressor, the enemy of the people. It will keep you cramped and insane your whole life, and it is the main obstacle between you and a shitty first draft. I think perfectionism is based on the obsessive belief that if you run carefully enough, hitting each stepping-stone just right, you won't have to die. The truth is that you will die anyway and that a lot of people who aren't even looking at their feet are going to do a whole lot better than you, and have a lot more fun while they're doing it.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/40088-perfectionism-is-the-voice-of-the-oppressor-the-enemy-of">1190 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
